I've uploaded a code repository in the directory . Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
[Provisioning Generator] Handle multiple resources sharing the same resource model
## Problem

The current implementation in `ProvisioningTypeFactory.CreateModelCore` assumes one resource model maps to exactly one resource definition (`ProvisioningResourceProvider`).

However, some management RPs have multiple ARM resources sharing the same resource model — in TypeSpec, there is only one model, but it is used in CRUD operations for multiple ARM resources with different resource types. Since the provisioning resource class has a resource type hard-coded inside it, we must generate multiple classes when this happens.

Additionally, other models might reference a resource model as a property type. If the model is shared across multiple resources, it's unclear which resource class to use as the property type.

## Location

- `ProvisioningTypeFactory.cs:171` — TODO comment
- `docs/design.md:183` — TODO note

## Related

- PR: https://github.com/Azure/azure-sdk-for-net/pull/56627


</pr_description>

     1	// Copyright (c) Microsoft Corporation. All rights reserved.
     2	// Licensed under the MIT License.
     3	
     4	using Azure.Generator.Management;
     5	using Azure.Generator.Provisioning.Primitives;
     6	using Azure.Generator.Provisioning.Providers;
     7	using Azure.Provisioning;
     8	using Azure.Provisioning.Primitives;
     9	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Input;
    10	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Input.Extensions;
    11	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Primitives;
    12	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Providers;
    13	using System;
    14	using System.Linq;
    15	
    16	namespace Azure.Generator.Provisioning
    17	{
    18	    /// <summary>
    19	    /// TypeFactory for provisioning generator that intercepts model/enum creation
    20	    /// to return provisioning-style type providers (ProvisionableConstruct/ProvisionableResource)
    21	    /// instead of management-style types.
    22	    /// </summary>
    23	    public class ProvisioningTypeFactory : ManagementTypeFactory
    24	    {
    25	        /// <summary>
    26	        /// Builds the resource provider name from the provisioning namespace.
    27	        /// For instance, "Azure.Provisioning.KeyVault" returns "KeyVault".
    28	        /// </summary>
    29	        protected override string BuildResourceProviderName()
    30	        {
    31	            const string provisioningNamespacePrefix = "Azure.Provisioning.";
    32	            if (PrimaryNamespace.StartsWith(provisioningNamespacePrefix))
    33	            {
    34	                return PrimaryNamespace[provisioningNamespacePrefix.Length..].ToIdentifierName();
    35	            }
    36	            return base.BuildResourceProviderName();
    37	        }
    38	
    39	        /// <inheritdoc/>
    40	        protected override CSharpType? CreateCSharpTypeCore(InputType inputType)
    41	        {
    42	            // For model types, check if there's a provisioning-specific type mapping first
    43	            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel
    44	                && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provisioningType))
    45	            {
    46	                return provisioningType;
    47	            }
    48	
    49	            // For enum types, check provisioning mapping too (e.g., ManagedServiceIdentityType)
    50	            if (inputType is InputEnumType inputEnum
    51	                && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputEnum.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provisioningEnumType))
    52	            {
    53	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), provisioningEnumType);
    54	            }
    55	
    56	            // Let the mgmt base resolve known system types (ResourceIdentifier, AzureLocation, etc.)
    57	            var mgmtType = base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
    58	
    59	            // For model types: if resolved to a system type that's a ProvisionableConstruct, return as-is.
    60	            // Otherwise, for non-ProvisionableConstruct system types (ResponseError from mgmt),
    61	            // wrap in BicepValue<T> since they can't be used with DefineModelProperty.
    62	            if (inputType is InputModelType)
    63	            {
    64	                if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
    65	                    && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
    66	                {
    67	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
    68	                }
    69	                return mgmtType;
    70	            }
    71	
    72	            // For enum types, wrap in BicepValue<T>
    73	            // System enums: mgmtType is the system CSharpType
    74	            // Non-system enums: mgmtType is our ProvisioningEnumProvider.Type
    75	            if (inputType is InputEnumType)
    76	            {
    77	                if (mgmtType != null)
    78	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
    79	                // Fallback: shouldn't happen now that ProvisioningEnumProvider is wired up
    80	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), typeof(string));
    81	            }
    82	
    83	            // For array types, produce BicepList<T> — element type should NOT be BicepValue-wrapped
    84	            if (inputType is InputArrayType arrayType)
    85	            {
    86	                var elementType = GetUnwrappedCSharpType(arrayType.ValueType);
    87	                if (elementType != null)
    88	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepList<>), elementType);
    89	            }
    90	
    91	            // For dictionary types, produce BicepDictionary<TValue> — value type should NOT be BicepValue-wrapped
    92	            if (inputType is InputDictionaryType dictType)
    93	            {
    94	                var valueType = GetUnwrappedCSharpType(dictType.ValueType);
    95	                if (valueType != null)
    96	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepDictionary<>), valueType);
    97	            }
    98	
    99	            // For all other non-model, non-enum types resolved by base (primitives, date/time, duration, etc.),
   100	            // wrap in BicepValue<T>
   101	            if (mgmtType != null)
   102	            {
   103	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
   104	            }
   105	
   106	            return mgmtType;
   107	        }
   108	
   109	        /// <summary>
   110	        /// Resolves an InputType to its raw CSharpType without BicepValue wrapping.
   111	        /// Used for BicepList/BicepDictionary element types which handle wrapping internally.
   112	        /// </summary>
   113	        private CSharpType? GetUnwrappedCSharpType(InputType inputType)
   114	        {
   115	            // For model types, check provisioning mapping first, then fall back to base
   116	            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel)
   117	            {
   118	                if (KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provType))
   119	                    return provType;
   120	                return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType) ?? CreateCSharpType(inputType);
   121	            }
   122	
   123	            // For enum types, check provisioning mapping first, then fall back to base
   124	            if (inputType is InputEnumType inputEnum)
   125	            {
   126	                if (KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputEnum.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provEnumType))
   127	                    return provEnumType;
   128	                return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType) ?? typeof(string);
   129	            }
   130	
   131	            // For all other types, use the base resolution (returns raw .NET type)
   132	            return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
   133	        }
   134	
   135	        /// <inheritdoc/>
   136	        protected override ModelProvider? CreateModelCore(InputModelType model)
   137	        {
   138	            // Known provisioning types (ManagedServiceIdentity, SystemData, etc.) → null (use framework type)
   139	            if (KnownProvisioningTypes.IsKnownType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId))
   140	                return null;
   141	
   142	            // Inheritable system types (TrackedResource, ProxyResource, etc.) → null
   143	            // Provisioning types use ProvisionableConstruct/ProvisionableResource as base, not ARM base types
   144	            if (KnownProvisioningTypes.IsInheritableSystemType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId))
   145	                return null;
   146	
   147	            // "Unknown" discriminator variants are for deserialization fallback in client SDKs.
   148	            // Provisioning types are write-only (compiled to Bicep), so we skip them.
   149	            if (model.IsUnknownDiscriminatorModel)
   150	                return null;
   151	
   152	            // Resource models → look up from output library's pre-created resource providers
   153	            var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
   154	            if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(model, out var resources))
   155	            {
   156	                if (resources.Count == 1)
   157	                {
   158	                    return resources[0];
   159	                }
   160	                // Multiple resources share the same model — not yet supported
   161	                throw new NotSupportedException(
   162	                    $"Model '{model.Name}' is shared by {resources.Count} resource types " +
   163	                    $"({string.Join(", ", resources.Select(r => r.Name))}). " +
   164	                    $"Multiple resources sharing the same model is not yet supported. " +
   165	                    $"See https://github.com/Azure/azure-sdk-for-net/issues/56733");
   166	            }
   167	
   168	            // Derived discriminated resource types → ProvisioningResourceProvider (derived path)
   169	            if (model.DiscriminatorValue != null && IsBaseChainResource(model))
   170	            {
   171	                return new ProvisioningResourceProvider(model);
   172	            }
   173	
   174	            // Regular models (including discriminated models) → ProvisioningModelProvider
   175	            return new ProvisioningModelProvider(model);
   176	        }
   177	
   178	        /// <summary>
   179	        /// Checks whether any model in the base chain is a resource model.
   180	        /// </summary>
   181	        private bool IsBaseChainResource(InputModelType model)
   182	        {
   183	            var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
   184	            var baseModel = model.BaseModel;
   185	            while (baseModel != null)
   186	            {
   187	                if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(baseModel, out _))
   188	                    return true;
   189	                baseModel = baseModel.BaseModel;
   190	            }
   191	            return false;
   192	        }
   193	
   194	        /// <inheritdoc/>
   195	        protected override EnumProvider? CreateEnumCore(InputEnumType enumType, TypeProvider? declaringType)
   196	        {
   197	            // Known provisioning enums → null (use framework type)
   198	            if (KnownProvisioningTypes.IsKnownType(enumType.CrossLanguageDefinitionId))
   199	                return null;
   200	
   201	            // Regular enums → ProvisioningEnumProvider
   202	            return new ProvisioningEnumProvider(enumType);
   203	        }
   204	
   205	        /// <inheritdoc/>
   206	        protected override PropertyProvider? CreatePropertyCore(InputProperty inputProperty, TypeProvider enclosingType)
   207	        {
   208	            // Run base chain which creates property and applies visitor renames (e.g., etag → ETag).
   209	            var baseProperty = base.CreatePropertyCore(inputProperty, enclosingType);
   210	
   211	            if (inputProperty is not InputModelProperty inputModelProperty)
   212	                return baseProperty;
   213	
   214	            if (enclosingType is IProvisioningPropertyInfo infoProvider)
   215	            {
   216	                var info = infoProvider.GetProvisioningPropertyInfo(inputModelProperty);
   217	                if (info == null) return null;
   218	                var resolvedName = baseProperty?.Name ?? info.PropertyName;
   219	                var bicepType = info.TypeOverride ?? CreateCSharpType(inputModelProperty.Type);
   220	                if (bicepType == null) return null;
   221	
   222	                return ProvisioningPropertyProvider.Create(
   223	                    resolvedName, bicepType,
   224	                    info.IsOutput, info.IsRequired, info.BicepPath, info.DefaultValue,
   225	                    enclosingType);
   226	            }
   227	
   228	            return baseProperty;
   229	        }
   230	    }
   231	}

OBSERVATION:

     1	# Provisioning Generator V2 — Design Document
     2	
     3	## 1. Background & Motivation
     4	
     5	### What is Azure.Provisioning?
     6	
     7	The `Azure.Provisioning.*` libraries provide a C# infrastructure-as-code experience for Azure resources. Each library wraps an Azure Resource Manager (ARM) resource type with `ProvisionableResource` subclasses that expose `BicepValue<T>` properties, enabling users to declare Azure resources in C# and compile them to Bicep templates.
     8	
     9	### Current Generator
    10	
    11	The current generator (`sdk/provisioning/Generator/src/`) is a standalone .NET console application that:
    12	
    13	1. **Takes NuGet packages as input** — references `Azure.ResourceManager.*` packages in its `.csproj`, loading compiled assemblies at runtime.
    14	2. **Uses .NET reflection** — introspects ARM SDK types (collections, resources, data classes) to discover resource shapes, properties, and parent-child relationships.
    15	3. **Extracts API versions from XML doc comments** — parses `<summary>` tags on ARM methods to find version strings like `2023-01-01`.
    16	4. **Requires a hand-written `Specification` class per service** — each service (Storage, KeyVault, etc.) needs a `*Specification.cs` file that registers the entry-point type, applies customizations (remove properties, rename models, add naming constraints, define RBAC roles), and is hard-coded in `Program.cs`.
    17	5. **Outputs `src/Generated/*.cs` files** — writes `ProvisionableResource` subclasses, model classes, enums, role definitions, and Bicep schema files.
    18	
    19	### Problems with the Current Approach
    20	
    21	| Problem | Impact |
    22	|---------|--------|
    23	| **NuGet dependency lag** | The generator reads from _published_ NuGet packages, not source. When an mgmt package is updated, the provisioning generator cannot pick up changes until a new NuGet version is published and referenced. |
    24	| **Hand-written Specification per service** | Every new provisioning library requires a developer to: (1) create a Specification class, (2) add the NuGet reference, (3) register in `Program.cs`. This does not scale. |
    25	| **Reflection is fragile** | The generator relies on internal patterns of the ARM SDK (e.g., finding `CreateOrUpdate` methods on `ArmCollection` types). Changes to ARM SDK codegen patterns silently break provisioning generation. |
    26	| **No TypeSpec integration** | As management plane SDKs migrate from Swagger/AutoRest to TypeSpec, the TypeSpec toolchain has richer semantic information (resource types, API versions, property metadata) that is lost when going through NuGet binaries. |
    27	| **Version discovery is indirect** | API versions are extracted from XML doc comment strings using regex, which is brittle and sometimes incorrect (e.g., preview versions leaking through). |
    28	| **No automation** | Generating a provisioning library is a fully manual process with no CI/CD integration. |
    29	
    30	### Why Now?
    31	
    32	Four provisioning libraries now have TypeSpec-based mgmt counterparts:
    33	
    34	| Provisioning Package | Mgmt Package | TypeSpec Spec Path |
    35	|---|---|---|
    36	| `Azure.Provisioning.AppConfiguration` | `Azure.ResourceManager.AppConfiguration` | `specification/appconfiguration/resource-manager/...` |
    37	| `Azure.Provisioning.KeyVault` | `Azure.ResourceManager.KeyVault` | `specification/keyvault/KeyVault.Management` |
    38	| `Azure.Provisioning.Kubernetes` | `Azure.ResourceManager.Kubernetes` | `specification/hybridkubernetes/...` |
    39	| `Azure.Provisioning.SignalR` | `Azure.ResourceManager.SignalR` | `specification/signalr/resource-manager/...` |
    40	
    41	As more management SDKs migrate to TypeSpec, this number will grow rapidly. Now is the right time to build a generator that integrates into the TypeSpec toolchain.
    42	
    43	---
    44	
    45	## 2. Goals & Non-Goals
    46	
    47	### Goals
    48	
    49	1. **Automate provisioning library generation from TypeSpec** — given a TypeSpec definition for a management-plane service, produce a complete `Azure.Provisioning.*` library with minimal manual intervention.
    50	2. **Eliminate hand-written Specification classes** — resource discovery, property extraction, parent-child relationships, and API versions should be derived automatically from the TypeSpec input model or the generated mgmt SDK.
    51	3. **Integrate into the existing TypeSpec emitter ecosystem** — leverage the layered emitter architecture (`http-client-csharp` → `http-client-csharp-mgmt` → provisioning) so that provisioning generation can be triggered alongside mgmt SDK generation.
    52	4. **Support customization without forking** — provide a declarative customization mechanism (e.g., a config file or decorators) for service-specific tweaks (naming overrides, property removal, RBAC roles, naming constraints).
    53	5. **Maintain backward compatibility** — generated output must be API-compatible with existing `Azure.Provisioning.*` libraries. Existing users should not experience breaking changes.
    54	6. **Support incremental adoption** — the new generator should coexist with the current one. Services can migrate individually from the old generator to the new one.
    55	
    56	### Non-Goals
    57	
    58	- **Replace the current generator immediately** — the 25 Swagger-based services will continue using the current generator until their mgmt packages migrate to TypeSpec.
    59	- **Generate provisioning libraries for data-plane services** — provisioning is management-plane only.
    60	- **Multi-language support** — the provisioning libraries are .NET-only.
    61	- **Generate test code** — tests remain hand-written.
    62	
    63	---
    64	
    65	## 3. Architecture
    66	
    67	The provisioning generator is built as a new TypeSpec emitter package that extends the management emitter — a new layer in the existing emitter stack:
    68	
    69	```
    70	@typespec/http-client-csharp                         (core)
    71	       ↑
    72	@azure-typespec/http-client-csharp                    (Azure base)
    73	       ↑
    74	@azure-typespec/http-client-csharp-mgmt               (ARM management)
    75	       ↑
    76	@azure-typespec/http-client-csharp-provisioning        (NEW — provisioning)
    77	```
    78	
    79	**How it works:**
    80	- Hooks into `$onEmit()` like the mgmt emitter.
    81	- Receives the full TypeSpec code model (resources, models, enums, operations, API versions).
    82	- Transforms the code model into provisioning-specific output (ProvisionableResource classes, BicepValue properties, etc.).
    83	- Runs a C# generator (`ProvisioningGenerator`, extending `ManagementClientGenerator`) that produces the provisioning `.cs` files.
    84	
    85	**Why this approach:**
    86	- First-class TypeSpec integration — accesses the richest semantic information.
    87	- API versions, resource types, and property metadata are directly available.
    88	- Can be triggered via `tsp compile` alongside mgmt SDK generation.
    89	- Follows the established emitter pattern used by the rest of the Azure SDK.
    90	
    91	**Challenges to address:**
    92	- The provisioning output is fundamentally different from a client SDK — it generates `ProvisionableResource` subclasses, not `ArmClient`/`ArmResource` types. This requires significant divergence in the C# generator's `TypeFactory` and `OutputLibrary`.
    93	- Tight coupling to the emitter release cadence.
    94	
    95	---
    96	
    97	## 4. Detailed Design
    98	
    99	### High-Level Architecture
   100	
   101	```
   102	@typespec/http-client-csharp                         (core emitter)
   103	       ↑
   104	@azure-typespec/http-client-csharp                    (Azure base emitter)
   105	       ↑
   106	@azure-typespec/http-client-csharp-mgmt               (ARM management emitter)
   107	       ↑
   108	@azure-typespec/http-client-csharp-provisioning        (provisioning emitter)
   109	```
   110	
   111	**Emitter side (TypeScript):**
   112	- Hooks into `$onEmit()`, setting `generator-name` to `ProvisioningGenerator`.
   113	- Delegates to the mgmt emitter, which passes the full code model to the C# generator.
   114	- Can apply provisioning-specific TypeSpec decorators or code model mutations if needed.
   115	
   116	**Generator side (C#):**
   117	- `ProvisioningGenerator` extends `ManagementClientGenerator`.
   118	- Overrides `TypeFactory` to produce provisioning-specific output types (`ProvisionableResource`, `BicepValue<T>` properties, etc.).
   119	- Overrides `OutputLibrary` to control which files are generated (provisioning classes instead of ARM client classes).
   120	- Reads the same code model (resources, models, enums, API versions) that the mgmt generator uses, but transforms it into provisioning output.
   121	
   122	```
   123	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   124	│                    TypeSpec Definitions                      │
   125	│           (azure-rest-api-specs repository)                  │
   126	└─────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────┘
   127	                      │
   128	                      ▼
   129	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   130	│        TypeSpec Emitter Chain                                │
   131	│                                                             │
   132	│  @typespec/http-client-csharp                               │
   133	│    → @azure-typespec/http-client-csharp                     │
   134	│      → @azure-typespec/http-client-csharp-mgmt              │
   135	│        → @azure-typespec/http-client-csharp-provisioning    │
   136	│                                                             │
   137	│  Output: Code model (tspCodeModel.json)                     │
   138	└─────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────┘
   139	                      │
   140	                      ▼
   141	┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   142	│              ProvisioningGenerator (C#)                      │
   143	│  (extends ManagementClientGenerator)                        │
   144	│                                                             │
   145	│  Pipeline:                                                  │
   146	│  1. Load code model from emitter                            │
   147	│  2. Override TypeFactory for provisioning types              │
   148	│  3. Override OutputLibrary for provisioning output           │
   149	│  4. Generate C# files:                                      │
   150	│     - ProvisionableResource subclasses                      │
   151	│     - BicepValue<T> property wrappers                       │
   152	│     - Model classes (ProvisionableConstruct subclasses)     │
   153	│     - Enum types                                            │
   154	│     - ResourceVersions nested classes                       │
   155	│     - Built-in role enums                                   │
   156	│                                                             │
   157	│  Output: Azure.Provisioning.*/src/Generated/*.cs            │
   158	└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
   159	```
   160	
   161	---
   162	
   163	## 5. TypeFactory & Type Resolution
   164	
   165	The provisioning generator uses **TypeFactory extension points** to intercept type creation at the framework level. This is the core architectural decision — instead of post-processing mgmt output, we replace type creation itself.
   166	
   167	### Overrides
   168	
   169	The `ProvisioningTypeFactory` extends `ManagementTypeFactory` and overrides four extension points: model creation, enum creation, C# type resolution, and property creation.
   170	
   171	- **Model creation** routes each input model type to the appropriate provisioning provider — resource models become `ProvisionableResource` subclasses, regular models become `ProvisionableConstruct` subclasses, and system/framework types are skipped (they come from the `Azure.Provisioning` base package).
   172	- **Enum creation** produces simple C# `enum` types instead of the extensible `readonly struct` pattern used by mgmt libraries.
   173	- **Type resolution** wraps scalar types in `BicepValue<T>`, arrays in `BicepList<T>`, and dictionaries in `BicepDictionary<T>`. Model types resolve to our providers without wrapping.
   174	- **Property creation** delegates to base to run the mgmt visitor pipeline (e.g., standard name renames like `Etag` → `ETag`), then creates a provisioning-style property with a linked backing field and `BicepValue` getter/setter.
   175	
   176	### Resource Detection
   177	
   178	Resource models are identified from the ARM provider schema at the input level. The output library pre-creates all resources from the schema at construction time, populating a map from input model types to resource metadata used by the factory.
   179	
   180	**Important:** We access the input-level resource schema and **never** the mgmt output library's resource providers, which would trigger model creation causing crashes since our factory returns provisioning types instead of the expected mgmt types.
   181	
   182	### Type Resolution Flow
   183	
   184	```
   185	InputModelType → Model creation
   186	  ├─ Known framework type? → null (use Azure.Provisioning base)
   187	  ├─ Inheritable system type? → null (e.g., ManagedServiceIdentity, SystemData)
   188	  ├─ ARM resource model? → ProvisioningResourceProvider
   189	  ├─ Discriminator variant of resource? → ProvisioningResourceProvider (derived)
   190	  └─ Regular model? → ProvisioningModelProvider
   191	
   192	InputType → Type resolution
   193	  ├─ Model type → provider's CSharpType (no wrapping)
   194	  ├─ Array → BicepList<elementType>
   195	  ├─ Dictionary → BicepDictionary<valueType>
   196	  ├─ Enum (system) → BicepValue<frameworkEnumType>
   197	  ├─ Enum (custom) → BicepValue<generatedEnumType>
   198	  └─ Scalar → BicepValue<T> (string, int, DateTimeOffset, ResourceIdentifier, etc.)
   199	```
   200	
   201	Element types for `BicepList<T>` and `BicepDictionary<T>` are resolved without `BicepValue<T>` wrapping (avoids `BicepList<BicepValue<string>>`).
   202	
   203	---
   204	
   205	## 6. Output Types
   206	
   207	### Resource Provider
   208	
   209	Generates `ProvisionableResource` subclasses from input model types + resource metadata:
   210	- **Property collection**: walks the model's inheritance chain and collects all properties, flattening only those with the `@flattenProperty` decorator
   211	- **Field-property linking**: each property gets a nullable backing field. Properties and fields are co-created through the TypeFactory property creation pipeline, ensuring names go through the mgmt visitor pipeline. These linked pairs are lazily initialized on first access.
   212	- **System properties**: `name`, `location` (required input), `id`, `systemData` (output-only), `tags` (input), `type` (skipped)
   213	- **Parent resources**: child resources get a typed `Parent` property for parent-child relationship
   214	- **Constructor**: `(string bicepIdentifier, string? resourceVersion)` with default API version
   215	- **`FromExisting()`**: static factory method
   216	- **`ResourceVersions`**: nested class with GA API version constants
   217	
   218	### Model Provider
   219	
   220	Generates `ProvisionableConstruct` subclasses:
   221	- Same field-property co-creation pattern as resources — properties go through the TypeFactory pipeline for visitor-based name resolution
   222	- Getter/setter patterns: models use `AssignOrReplace`, BicepValue types use `.Assign()`, read-only properties are getter-only
   223	- `DefineProvisionableProperties()` maps each property to its bicep path
   224	
   225	### Enum Provider
   226	
   227	Generates simple C# `enum` types:
   228	- Optional `[DataMember(Name = "...")]` attribute when the serialized value differs from the member name
   229	- No serialization providers — provisioning enums are serialized via `DefineProperty` at the resource/model level
   230	
   231	### Output Library
   232	
   233	The output library bypasses the mgmt output pipeline (which would trigger mgmt-specific type initialization) and instead iterates input models and enums directly, routing each through our TypeFactory. Only resources are marked as "types to keep" — the post-processor automatically prunes unreferenced models and enums.
   234	
   235	---
   236	
   237	## 7. Naming & Namespace Strategy
   238	
   239	- All types in flat namespace: `Azure.Provisioning.{ServiceName}` (no `.Models` sub-namespace)
   240	- Achieved by setting `model-namespace=false` in the provisioning emitter, which prevents the base `NamespaceVisitor` from appending `.Models`
   241	- Resource model names have the "Data" suffix stripped by `ResourceDataSuffixVisitor` — the mgmt `ResourceVisitor` appends "Data" (e.g., `ConfigurationStore` → `ConfigurationStoreData`), and our visitor reverts it since provisioning libraries don't use the Data suffix convention
   242	- Property names are resolved through the `TypeFactory.CreatePropertyCore()` pipeline, which runs mgmt visitors (specifically `NameVisitor`) to apply standard renames: `Etag` → `ETag`, `CreationDate` → `CreatedOn`, `*Url` → `*Uri`, and other datetime suffix normalizations. This ensures provisioning libraries follow the same naming conventions as mgmt libraries without duplicating rename rules.
   243	
   244	---
   245	
   246	## 8. Migration Strategy
   247	
   248	The new emitter-based generator coexists with the current reflection-based generator:
   249	
   250	```

2026-06-01 03:30:43,170 - INFO - swea-agent-Azure__azure-sdk-for-net-58482 - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:

     1	// Copyright (c) Microsoft Corporation. All rights reserved.
     2	// Licensed under the MIT License.
     3	
     4	using System;
     5	using System.Reflection;
     6	using Azure.Generator.Management;
     7	using Azure.Generator.Provisioning.Providers;
     8	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Input;
     9	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Providers;
    10	using System.Collections.Generic;
    11	using System.Linq;
    12	
    13	namespace Azure.Generator.Provisioning
    14	{
    15	    /// <summary>
    16	    /// Output library for provisioning generator. Pre-creates all resource providers
    17	    /// from ArmProviderSchema.Resources and builds model/enum providers from input types.
    18	    /// </summary>
    19	    public class ProvisioningOutputLibrary : ManagementOutputLibrary
    20	    {
    21	        private IReadOnlyList<ProvisioningResourceProvider>? _resources;
    22	        private Dictionary<string, ProvisioningResourceProvider>? _resourcesByIdPattern;
    23	        private Dictionary<InputModelType, List<ProvisioningResourceProvider>>? _resourcesByModel;
    24	        private BuiltInRoleProvider? _builtInRole;
    25	
    26	        /// <summary>
    27	        /// Gets the BuiltInRole type provider if any resources define RBAC roles.
    28	        /// </summary>
    29	        internal BuiltInRoleProvider? BuiltInRole => GetNullableValue(ref _builtInRole);
    30	
    31	        private T GetValue<T>(ref T? field) where T : class
    32	        {
    33	            InitializeResources(ref _resources, ref _resourcesByIdPattern, ref _resourcesByModel, ref _builtInRole);
    34	            return field!;
    35	        }
    36	
    37	        private T? GetNullableValue<T>(ref T? field) where T : class
    38	        {
    39	            InitializeResources(ref _resources, ref _resourcesByIdPattern, ref _resourcesByModel, ref _builtInRole);
    40	            return field;
    41	        }
    42	
    43	        /// <summary>
    44	        /// Gets all provisioning resource providers.
    45	        /// </summary>
    46	        internal IReadOnlyList<ProvisioningResourceProvider> Resources => GetValue(ref _resources);
    47	
    48	        private void InitializeResources(
    49	            ref IReadOnlyList<ProvisioningResourceProvider>? resources,
    50	            ref Dictionary<string, ProvisioningResourceProvider>? resourcesByIdPattern,
    51	            ref Dictionary<InputModelType, List<ProvisioningResourceProvider>>? resourcesByModel,
    52	            ref BuiltInRoleProvider? builtInRole)
    53	        {
    54	            if (resources != null)
    55	                return;
    56	
    57	            var list = new List<ProvisioningResourceProvider>();
    58	            var byIdPattern = new Dictionary<string, ProvisioningResourceProvider>();
    59	            var byModel = new Dictionary<InputModelType, List<ProvisioningResourceProvider>>();
    60	
    61	            var allMetadata = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.InputLibrary.ArmProviderSchema.Resources;
    62	            foreach (var metadata in allMetadata)
    63	            {
    64	                if (metadata.ResourceModel == null)
    65	                    continue;
    66	
    67	                var resource = new ProvisioningResourceProvider(metadata.ResourceModel, metadata);
    68	                list.Add(resource);
    69	                byIdPattern[metadata.ResourceIdPattern] = resource;
    70	
    71	                if (!byModel.TryGetValue(metadata.ResourceModel, out var modelList))
    72	                {
    73	                    modelList = new List<ProvisioningResourceProvider>();
    74	                    byModel[metadata.ResourceModel] = modelList;
    75	                }
    76	                modelList.Add(resource);
    77	            }
    78	
    79	            // Initialize BuiltInRole from input metadata — this is safe to do here since
    80	            // it's constructed purely from input values, and must be available before any
    81	            // resource provider's methods are materialized.
    82	            var serviceName = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.TypeFactory.ResourceProviderName;
    83	            builtInRole = BuiltInRoleProvider.TryCreate(serviceName, allMetadata);
    84	
    85	            resources = list;
    86	            resourcesByIdPattern = byIdPattern;
    87	            resourcesByModel = byModel;
    88	        }
    89	
    90	        /// <summary>
    91	        /// Tries to get the resource provider(s) for a given InputModelType.
    92	        /// Returns false if the model is not a resource model.
    93	        /// </summary>
    94	        internal bool TryGetResourcesByModel(InputModelType model, out IReadOnlyList<ProvisioningResourceProvider> resources)
    95	        {
    96	            if (GetValue(ref _resourcesByModel).TryGetValue(model, out var list))
    97	            {
    98	                resources = list;
    99	                return true;
   100	            }
   101	            resources = [];
   102	            return false;
   103	        }
   104	
   105	        /// <summary>
   106	        /// Gets a resource provider by its ARM resource ID pattern.
   107	        /// Returns null if not found.
   108	        /// </summary>
   109	        internal ProvisioningResourceProvider? GetResourceByIdPattern(string resourceIdPattern)
   110	        {
   111	            GetValue(ref _resourcesByIdPattern).TryGetValue(resourceIdPattern, out var resource);
   112	            return resource;
   113	        }
   114	
   115	        /// <inheritdoc/>
   116	        protected override TypeProvider[] BuildTypeProviders()
   117	        {
   118	            // TODO: Ideally we should call base.BuildTypeProviders() and filter the results
   119	            // to keep only models, enums, and CodeGen attributes. However, ManagementOutputLibrary
   120	            // eagerly initializes mgmt-specific client types (ResourceClientProvider,
   121	            // ResourceCollectionClientProvider, etc.) whose BuildMethods() crashes because
   122	            // our provisioning models don't have paging properties like 'nextLink'.
   123	            // Until ManagementOutputLibrary is refactored to support lazy initialization or
   124	            // allows skipping client type construction, we build the provider list manually.
   125	
   126	            var providers = new List<TypeProvider>();
   127	
   128	            // Add resource providers and mark them to survive post-processing.
   129	            foreach (var resource in Resources)
   130	            {
   131	                providers.Add(resource);
   132	                ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.AddTypeToKeep(resource.Name);
   133	            }
   134	
   135	            // Add BuiltInRole struct if any resources have RBAC roles defined.
   136	            if (BuiltInRole != null)
   137	            {
   138	                providers.Add(BuiltInRole);
   139	            }
   140	
   141	            // Build models and enums via TypeFactory — our overridden CreateModel/CreateEnum
   142	            // return ProvisioningModelProvider/ProvisioningResourceProvider/EnumProvider.
   143	            var inputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.InputLibrary;
   144	            foreach (var inputModel in inputLib.InputNamespace.Models)
   145	            {
   146	                var model = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.TypeFactory.CreateModel(inputModel);
   147	                if (model is not null && model is not ProvisioningResourceProvider)
   148	                {
   149	                    providers.Add(model);
   150	                }
   151	            }
   152	
   153	            foreach (var inputEnum in inputLib.InputNamespace.Enums)
   154	            {
   155	                var enumProvider = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.TypeFactory.CreateEnum(inputEnum);
   156	                if (enumProvider != null)
   157	                {
   158	                    providers.Add(enumProvider);
   159	                }
   160	            }
   161	
   162	            // TODO: CodeGen* attribute definitions (CodeGenType, CodeGenMember, etc.) are
   163	            // included in base OutputLibrary.BuildTypeProviders() via the internal property
   164	            // CodeModelGenerator.CustomCodeAttributeProviders. Since we can't call base and
   165	            // the property is inaccessible, we discover them by convention using reflection.
   166	            // This should be replaced by a base.BuildTypeProviders() call once the above
   167	            // ManagementOutputLibrary issue is resolved.
   168	            foreach (var type in typeof(TypeProvider).Assembly.GetTypes())
   169	            {
   170	                if (typeof(TypeProvider).IsAssignableFrom(type)
   171	                    && !type.IsAbstract
   172	                    && type.Name.EndsWith("AttributeDefinition"))
   173	                {
   174	                    if (Activator.CreateInstance(type) is TypeProvider attrProvider)
   175	                    {
   176	                        providers.Add(attrProvider);
   177	                    }
   178	                }
   179	            }
   180	
   181	            return [.. providers];
   182	        }
   183	    }
   184	}

    30	    /// <summary>
    31	    /// Generates a ProvisionableResource subclass from an InputModelType + ArmResourceMetadata.
    32	    /// Flattens the ARM "properties" bag, includes system properties from the base model chain,
    33	    /// and generates ResourceVersions, FromExisting, and the resource constructor.
    34	    /// </summary>
    35	    internal class ProvisioningResourceProvider : ModelProvider, IProvisioningPropertyInfo
    36	    {
    37	        // System properties that should always be output-only
    38	        private static readonly HashSet<string> OutputOnlyProperties = new(StringComparer.OrdinalIgnoreCase)
    39	        {
    40	            "id", "systemData", "type"
    41	        };
    42	
    43	        // System properties that should always be required, even when marked readOnly (path parameters)
    44	        private static readonly HashSet<string> RequiredInputProperties = new(StringComparer.OrdinalIgnoreCase)
    45	        {
    46	            "name"
    47	        };
    48	
    49	        // Properties to skip entirely (type is implied by the resource type)
    50	        private static readonly HashSet<string> SkipProperties = new(StringComparer.OrdinalIgnoreCase)
    51	        {
    52	            "type"
    53	        };

    56	        private readonly ArmResourceMetadata? _resourceMetadata;
    57	        private readonly string? _defaultApiVersion;

    59	        /// All collected properties for the resource, including flattened and inherited ones,
    60	        /// with their resolved isOutput/isRequired/bicepPath metadata.
    61	        /// Used to build the C# Properties, Fields, and DefineProvisionableProperties() method.
    62	        /// </summary>

    64	        /// <summary>

    67	        /// </summary>
    68	        private readonly Dictionary<InputModelProperty, ResourcePropertyInfo> _propertyLookup;
    69	        /// <summary>
    70	        /// Serialized property names that are writable in the create/update request body model.
    71	        /// When the resource model is output-only (e.g., a ProxyResource with a separate create body),
    72	        /// its properties may be marked readOnly even though the create body accepts them as input.
    73	        /// This set is used during <see cref="_allProperties"/> construction to avoid incorrectly
    74	        /// marking such properties as output-only.
    75	        /// </summary>
    76	        private readonly HashSet<string> _createBodyWritableProperties;

    79	        private PropertyProvider? _parentProperty;
    80	        private CSharpType? _parentType;
