Now I have a clearer picture. Let me look at the `BuildTypeProviders` again:

When `BuildTypeProviders` runs:
1. It adds all `Resources` (one `ProvisioningResourceProvider` per `ArmResourceMetadata`)
2. It iterates all input models and calls `CreateModel`. For models that are resource models (single resource), `CreateModel` returns the already-created `ProvisioningResourceProvider`, which is filtered out. For non-resource models, it returns `ProvisioningModelProvider`.

Now for multi-resource case, the flow should be:
1. All `N` resource providers are added from `Resources` (already working)
2. When `CreateModel` is called for the shared model, it should return... something. 

If we look at the single-resource case: `CreateModel` returns the single `ProvisioningResourceProvider` for that model. This is used in:
- `BuildTypeProviders` - to filter it out
- `ProvisioningResourceProvider.BuildBaseType()` - for derived discriminated resources
- `CreateCSharpTypeCore` for model types - to resolve property types

For multi-resource case:
- `BuildTypeProviders` - if we return null, the model will be created as `ProvisioningModelProvider` (bad — duplicate properties)
- If we return the first resource, it works for type resolution but we lose the other resources

Actually, wait. Let me re-read `BuildTypeProviders` more carefully:

```csharp
foreach (var inputModel in inputLib.InputNamespace.Models)
{
    var model = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.TypeFactory.CreateModel(inputModel);
    if (model is not null && model is not ProvisioningResourceProvider)
    {
        providers.Add(model);
    }
}
```

If `CreateModel` returns null, the model is skipped entirely (not added as any provider). But the resource providers are already in the list! The model properties are already embedded in each `ProvisioningResourceProvider`. So we don't need a separate `ProvisioningModelProvider`.

But what about other models that reference this shared model as a property type? If another model has a property of this shared model type, `CreateCSharpTypeCore` would be called for it. Currently it goes to `base.CreateCSharpTypeCore` which calls `CreateModel`. If `CreateModel` returns null, then `base.CreateCSharpTypeCore` returns null, and then the method falls through... Let me trace through `CreateCSharpTypeCore`:

```csharp
protected override CSharpType? CreateCSharpTypeCore(InputType inputType)
{
    // For model types, check if there's a provisioning-specific type mapping first
    if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel
        && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provisioningType))
    {
        return provisioningType;
    }
    ...
    var mgmtType = base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
    ...
}
```

`base.CreateCSharpTypeCore` for `ManagementTypeFactory` would call `CreateModel` internally. If `CreateModel` returns null, then `mgmtType` is null. Then the code falls through to:

```csharp
if (inputType is InputModelType)
{
    if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
        && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
    {
        return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
    }
    return mgmtType;
}
```

If `mgmtType` is null, it returns null. That means the property referencing this shared model would have no type — that's a problem.

So the approach should be: when multiple resources share the same model, `CreateModelCore` should still return a model provider. But which one? 

I think the answer is: there should be a "base" model (a `ProvisionableConstruct`) that represents the shared data model, and each resource gets its own `ProvisionableResource` subclass that wraps/references this data model. But that seems like a big architectural change.

Alternatively, maybe the simpler approach: when multiple resources share the same model, `CreateModelCore` should pick ONE of them (maybe the first one) to represent the model type for property resolution purposes, and all the resource classes are still generated separately.

2026-06-01 03:42:42,790 - INFO - swea-agent-Azure__azure-sdk-for-net-58482 - 💭 THOUGHT
Let me think about this more practically. The PR description says:

1. **Multiple resources sharing the same model → generate multiple classes** 
   - Currently throws NotSupportedException
   - Should instead generate multiple `ProvisioningResourceProvider` classes, each with different resource types

2. **Other models referencing a resource model as property type** 
   - If the model is shared across multiple resources, it's unclear which resource class to use

Looking at the current code flow:

1. `ProvisioningOutputLibrary.InitializeResources()` creates one `ProvisioningResourceProvider` per `ArmResourceMetadata`, keyed by `InputModelType`. When multiple resources share the same model, `_resourcesByModel` maps the model to a list of resources.

2. In `BuildTypeProviders`, all resources from `Resources` are added first.

3. Then for each input model, `CreateModel` is called. If it's a resource model with a single resource, it returns that resource (which is filtered out). If multiple resources, it throws.

The fix should:
- In `CreateModelCore`, when multiple resources share the same model, **return null** (since the resources are already added directly from the `Resources` list). This way the model won't be created as a `ProvisioningModelProvider` either.
- But then property type resolution for this model would return null from `CreateModelCore`, which causes issues.

Actually, let me re-read the property resolution path. In `CreateCSharpTypeCore`:

```csharp
if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel
    && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(...))
{
    return provisioningType;
}
...
var mgmtType = base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
```

`base.CreateCSharpTypeCore` for `ManagementTypeFactory` ultimately calls `CreateModel` which calls `CreateModelCore`. If `CreateModelCore` returns null, then `mgmtType` is null, and the method returns null. Then in `CreatePropertyCore`, if `bicepType` is null, the property is skipped (returns null).

So for the multi-resource case, if we return null from `CreateModelCore`, properties that reference this model type would be skipped. That's not ideal.

Maybe the approach should be: when there are multiple resources sharing the model, return the first resource from `CreateModelCore` (as the "primary" resource type). This way:
1. The model is still recognized as a resource model
2. Property type resolution works (returns the primary resource type)
3. All resource classes are still generated (from the `Resources` loop)

But which resource should be the "primary"? Maybe we need to think about this differently.

Wait, let me look at the actual linked PR description more carefully. It says:

> Since the provisioning resource class has a resource type hard-coded inside it, we must generate multiple classes when this happens.

So the fix is about generating multiple classes. Currently, the code throws. The fix should allow multiple classes.

> Additionally, other models might reference a resource model as a property type. If the model is shared across multiple resources, it's unclear which resource class to use as the property type.

This is about the second problem. If model A is shared by resources R1 and R2, and model B has a property of type model A, what type should that property be?

I think the solution from the actual PR (azure-sdk-for-net#56627) might be:
1. When multiple resources share a model, still generate all resource classes
2. For the shared model itself, also create a `ProvisioningModelProvider` (a `ProvisionableConstruct`) as the data model
3. For properties referencing the shared model, use the `ProvisioningModelProvider` type (not any specific resource type)

But that would mean the `ProvisioningResourceProvider` and `ProvisioningModelProvider` both exist for the same model, which seems redundant.

Actually, let me look at this from the Azure.Provisioning library perspective. In the provisioning pattern:
- A `ProvisionableResource` extends `ProvisionableConstruct` (or `Resource` which extends `ProvisionableConstruct`)
- It has properties like Name, Location, etc. plus the resource-specific properties
- The resource-specific properties come from the resource's data model

When multiple resources share the same data model, they should share the same property definitions. The way to handle this is:
1. Generate a `ProvisioningModelProvider` for the shared data model (which becomes a `ProvisionableConstruct`)
2. Generate multiple `ProvisioningResourceProvider` classes that each extend `ProvisionableResource` and contain the same properties as the data model
3. For property type references, use the `ProvisioningModelProvider` type

But currently, `ProvisioningResourceProvider` directly includes all properties from the model. It doesn't reference a separate data model class.

Let me look at this from yet another angle. Let me check if there's a simpler approach: maybe just return null from `CreateModelCore` when multiple resources exist, and handle the property type resolution differently.

    39	        /// to the format for correct serialization of ManagedServiceIdentity.
    40	        /// </summary>
    41	        internal bool UseManagedServiceIdentityV3 => _useManagedServiceIdentityV3 ??= DetectManagedServiceIdentityV3();
    42	
    43	        private bool DetectManagedServiceIdentityV3()
    44	        {
    45	            var inputEnums = ManagementClientGenerator.Instance.InputLibrary.InputNamespace.Enums;
    46	            var identityTypeEnum = inputEnums.FirstOrDefault(e =>
    47	                e.CrossLanguageDefinitionId == "Azure.ResourceManager.CommonTypes.ManagedServiceIdentityType");
    48	            if (identityTypeEnum == null)
    49	                return false;
    50	            return identityTypeEnum.Values.Any(v =>
    51	                v.Value?.ToString() == "SystemAssigned,UserAssigned");
    52	        }

    65	        {

    67	            if (PrimaryNamespace.StartsWith(armNamespacePrefix))
    68	            {
    69	                return PrimaryNamespace[armNamespacePrefix.Length..].ToIdentifierName();
    70	            }

    72	        }

    89	        {
    90	            if (inputType is InputModelType model)
    91	            {
    92	                if (KnownManagementTypes.TryGetInheritableSystemType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var inheritableType))
    93	                {
    94	                    return inheritableType;
    95	                }
    96	                if (KnownManagementTypes.TryGetSystemType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var systemType))
    97	                {
    98	                    return systemType;
    99	                }
   100	            }
   101	
   102	            if (inputType is InputEnumType enumType && KnownManagementTypes.TryGetSystemType(enumType.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var replacedType))
   103	            {
   104	                return replacedType;
   105	            }
   106	
   107	            if (inputType is InputPrimitiveType primitiveType && KnownManagementTypes.TryGetPrimitiveType(primitiveType.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var primitiveReplacedType))
   108	            {
   109	                return primitiveReplacedType;
   110	            }
   111	            return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
   112	        }
   113	
   114	        /// <inheritdoc/>
   115	        protected override ModelProvider? CreateModelCore(InputModelType model)
   116	        {
   117	            // First check for standard ARM types that map to system types
   118	            if (KnownManagementTypes.TryGetInheritableSystemType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var replacedType))
   119	            {
   120	                return InheritableSystemObjectModelProvider.CreateSystemBase(replacedType.FrameworkType, model);
   121	            }
   122	            if (KnownManagementTypes.TryGetSystemType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out _))
   123	            {
   124	                return null;
   125	            }
   126	
   127	            // For models whose base is an inheritable system type (e.g., TrackedResource → TrackedResourceData),
   128	            // use a derived InheritableSystemObjectModelProvider which overrides BuildBaseType() to return the
   129	            // correct framework CSharpType. The default ModelProvider.BuildBaseType() returns
   130	            // BaseModelProvider.Type, which produces a non-framework CSharpType that gets eagerly cached.
   131	            if (model.BaseModel is { } baseModel &&
   132	                KnownManagementTypes.TryGetInheritableSystemType(baseModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var inheritableType))
   133	            {
   134	                CreateModel(baseModel);
   135	                return InheritableSystemObjectModelProvider.CreateDerived(model, inheritableType);
   136	            }
   137	
   138	            // For custom Azure resource models (root, intermediate, and resource data models),
   139	            // let the base implementation create regular ModelProviders.
   140	            // This preserves the full custom resource hierarchy without replacing intermediate
   141	            // models with system types (e.g., TrafficResource → TrafficProxyResource → TrafficEndpointData).
   142	            return base.CreateModelCore(model);
   143	        }

   157	        {
   158	            if (KnownManagementTypes.TryGetJsonSerializationExpression(valueType, out var serializationExpression))
   159	            {
   160	                return serializationExpression(valueType, value, utf8JsonWriter, mrwOptionsParameter, serializationFormat);
   161	            }

   174	                return value.CastTo(new CSharpType(typeof(IJsonModel<>), valueType)).Invoke(nameof(IJsonModel<object>.Write), [utf8JsonWriter, optionsArg]).Terminate();
   175	            }
   176	
   177	            return base.SerializeJsonValue(valueType, value, utf8JsonWriter, mrwOptionsParameter, serializationFormat);
   178	        }

   214	                            ])
   215	                    ]),
   216	                    wireOptions
   217	                ];
   218	
   219	                return Static(typeof(ModelReaderWriter)).Invoke(

   221	                    [.. readBody, ModelReaderWriterContextSnippets.Default],

   223	            }

2026-06-01 03:43:33,562 - INFO - swea-agent-Azure__azure-sdk-for-net-58482 - 💭 THOUGHT
The base class is likely from a compiled DLL. Let me look at how `CreateCSharpTypeCore` resolves model types by checking the `ProvisioningTypeFactory` again and tracing through logic.

Actually, let me take a step back. I've been analyzing the code extensively. Now let me formulate the solution:

**The Problem:**
1. `CreateModelCore` throws `NotSupportedException` when multiple resources share the same model.
2. Property type resolution for shared models is ambiguous.

**The Solution:**
Looking at how the code works:
- All resource providers are already generated from `Resources` list in `BuildTypeProviders`
- `CreateModelCore` is called for each model to determine if it's a resource model (returns `ProvisioningResourceProvider`) or a regular model (falls through to `ProvisioningModelProvider`)
- For single-resource models, it returns the resource provider (which is filtered out in `BuildTypeProviders` since it's already added)
- For multi-resource models, we should still return a model provider — but which one?

The key insight from the PR: "Since the provisioning resource class has a resource type hard-coded inside it, we must generate multiple classes when this happens."

So the fix should:
1. Generate multiple `ProvisioningResourceProvider` classes (already done via `Resources` loop)
2. In `CreateModelCore`, when there are multiple resources for a model, return `null` so the model is NOT treated as a single resource model

But then we need to handle property type resolution. Let me trace through what happens when a property references a model type:

`CreateCSharpTypeCore(InputType inputType)`:
- If it's an `InputModelType`, first checks `KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType` → might match
- For resource models that are NOT known types, calls `base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType)` → `ManagementTypeFactory.CreateCSharpTypeCore` → checks `KnownManagementTypes` → calls `base.CreateCSharpTypeCore` → `AzureTypeFactory.CreateCSharpTypeCore` → calls `CreateModel` → `CreateModelCore`

If `CreateModelCore` returns null, `CreateModel` returns null, `CreateCSharpTypeCore` returns null. Then back in `ProvisioningTypeFactory.CreateCSharpTypeCore`:
```csharp
var mgmtType = base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType); // null
...
if (inputType is InputModelType)
{
    if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType ...) { ... }
    return mgmtType; // returns null!
}
```

So property with type = shared resource model → null type → skipped.

This is the second problem described in the PR: "other models might reference a resource model as a property type. If the model is shared across multiple resources, it's unclear which resource class to use as the property type."

I think the solution for this is: when multiple resources share the same model, we should return the **first** resource's type as the representative type. This way:
1. Properties referencing the model get a valid type
2. All resource classes are still generated

But actually, wait. Let me look more carefully. Maybe the approach should be to generate a `ProvisioningModelProvider` for the shared model, and have each resource "wrap" it. But that would be a major refactor.

Let me look at what `ProvisioningResourceProvider` actually does with the model vs what `ProvisioningModelProvider` does:

- `ProvisioningResourceProvider`: Generates a `ProvisionableResource` subclass. It collects all properties from the model chain, flattens the "properties" bag, adds system properties (name, location, etc.), and generates `FromExisting()`, `ResourceVersions`, etc.
- `ProvisioningModelProvider`: Generates a `ProvisionableConstruct` subclass. It collects all properties from the model chain but doesn't add system properties or resource-specific methods.

If a model is shared by multiple resources, we want:
1. Each resource to have its own `ProvisionableResource` subclass (with its own resource type, API versions, etc.)
2. The shared data model properties to be available on each resource

Currently, each `ProvisioningResourceProvider` from the `Resources` list already has all properties from the model. So the properties are duplicated across resource classes. That's fine for code generation — each resource class will have the same set of properties.

For property type resolution: if another model has a property of the shared model type, which resource class should be used? The answer might be: it depends. But practically, we need to pick one. I think picking the first one is a reasonable approach, or we could create a separate "data model" class.

But wait, let me re-read the PR description: "Since the provisioning resource class has a resource type hard-coded inside it, we must generate multiple classes when this happens."

This confirms: multiple classes should be generated. The current code already generates multiple classes from the `Resources` loop. The only issue is that `CreateModelCore` throws when it sees multiple resources for the same model.

And: "Additionally, other models might reference a resource model as a property type. If the model is shared across multiple resources, it's unclear which resource class to use as the property type."

This is saying there's an ambiguity problem. But I think the solution for now is to:
1. Remove the `throw` and instead return `null` (or one of the resources)
2. Handle the property type resolution appropriately

Let me look at the approach more practically. Let me see if there are tests that indicate expected behavior:

2026-06-01 03:44:23,860 - INFO - swea-agent-Azure__azure-sdk-for-net-58482 - 💭 THOUGHT
I see `WorkbookTemplateGallery.cs` and `WorkbookTemplateLocalizedGallery.cs` — these are models. But there's no shared data model for Workbook and WorkbookTemplate.

Let me now formulate my understanding and the fix:

Based on the PR description, the issue is:
1. `CreateModelCore` throws `NotSupportedException` when multiple resources share the same model
2. This should instead handle the case gracefully

Looking at the code flow again:
- `BuildTypeProviders` already adds all `ProvisioningResourceProvider` instances from `Resources`
- `CreateModelCore` should handle the multi-resource case by returning `null` (since resources are already added)
- But for property type resolution, we need to return something meaningful

Let me check if there's a `ProvisioningResourceProvider` constructor that could be used to create a "model-only" provider (without resource metadata). Actually, looking at `ProvisioningResourceProvider`, there are two constructors:
1. `ProvisioningResourceProvider(InputModelType inputModel, ArmResourceMetadata metadata)` - for base resources
2. `internal ProvisioningResourceProvider(InputModelType inputModel)` - for derived discriminated resources

The second constructor creates a resource provider without metadata, which generates a derived discriminated resource type.

For the multi-resource case, the model itself should perhaps be generated as a `ProvisioningModelProvider` (a `ProvisionableConstruct`), not as a resource. Then each resource provider can reference it.

But wait, looking at `BuildTypeProviders`:
```csharp
foreach (var resource in Resources)
{
    providers.Add(resource);
    ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.AddTypeToKeep(resource.Name);
}
...
foreach (var inputModel in inputLib.InputNamespace.Models)
{
    var model = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.TypeFactory.CreateModel(inputModel);
    if (model is not null && model is not ProvisioningResourceProvider)
    {
        providers.Add(model);
    }
}
```

If `CreateModelCore` returns `null` for a multi-resource model, the model won't be added as any provider. But the resources are already added from the first loop. The resources contain all properties from the model. So the model properties are still generated, just inside each resource class.

For property type resolution: when another model references this shared model, we need a type to use. If we return `null` from `CreateModelCore`, the type resolution fails.

I think the solution is:
1. When multiple resources share the same model, `CreateModelCore` should return `null` (since resources are already added)
2. In `CreateCSharpTypeCore`, when resolving a model type that has multiple resources, we should pick the first resource's type (or maybe create a special handling)

Actually wait, let me look at the `ProvisioningTypeFactory.CreateCSharpTypeCore` again more carefully:

```csharp
protected override CSharpType? CreateCSharpTypeCore(InputType inputType)
{
    if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel
        && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provisioningType))
    {
        return provisioningType;
    }
    ...
    var mgmtType = base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
    
    if (inputType is InputModelType)
    {
        if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
            && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
        {
            return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
        }
        return mgmtType;
    }
    ...
}
```

`base.CreateCSharpTypeCore` calls `ManagementTypeFactory.CreateCSharpTypeCore` which calls `base.CreateCSharpTypeCore` which ultimately calls `CreateModel`. If `CreateModel` returns null, `mgmtType` is null, and `CreateCSharpTypeCore` returns null.

So for the multi-resource case, if we return null from `CreateModelCore`, property types referencing this model will be null, and properties will be skipped.

I think the PR's solution might be different. Let me think about what makes sense:

**Option A**: Return the first resource from `CreateModelCore` when there are multiple. This means:
- One resource is chosen as the "primary" resource type
- Properties referencing the model get the primary resource's type
- All resources are still generated from the `Resources` loop
- The model is still filtered out in `BuildTypeProviders` (since it returns a `ProvisioningResourceProvider`)

**Option B**: Return `null` from `CreateModelCore`, and also create a `ProvisioningModelProvider` for the shared model. This means:
- The model becomes a `ProvisionableConstruct` 
- Each resource becomes a `ProvisionableResource`
- Properties referencing the model get the `ProvisionableConstruct` type

But Option B would require significant changes to `BuildTypeProviders` to handle the case where a model is both a resource model (has resources) and a regular model (needs a `ProvisioningModelProvider`).

Let me look at what happens with Option A more carefully. If we return `resources[0]` from `CreateModelCore`:
- In `BuildTypeProviders`, `CreateModel` returns `resources[0]` which is a `ProvisioningResourceProvider`. It's filtered out (not added again).
- In property type resolution, `base.CreateCSharpTypeCore` → `CreateModel` → returns `resources[0]` → its `Type` is used as the property type.
- For derived discriminated resources that have this model as base, `CreateModel` returns `resources[0]` which works.

But wait, is there an issue with `BuildTypeProviders`? It already added all resources from `Resources`. Then when iterating models, `CreateModel` for the shared model returns `resources[0]`, which is already in the list. It's filtered out. Good.

But what about the OTHER resources (resources[1], resources[2], etc.)? They were already added from `Resources` loop. So they'll be generated too. Good.

So Option A seems to work. But which resource should be returned? The first one is arbitrary. The PR description mentions "it's unclear which resource class to use as the property type." So maybe the answer is: it doesn't matter which one we pick, as long as we pick one consistently.

Actually, wait. Let me re-think. The PR description says:

> Additionally, other models might reference a resource model as a property type. If the model is shared across multiple resources, it's unclear which resource class to use as the property type.

This sounds like a caveat/known issue, not something that needs to be solved. The main fix is:
1. Generate multiple classes when multiple resources share the same model
2. For property type references, pick one (maybe the first)

Let me now implement the fix. The change should be in `ProvisioningTypeFactory.cs`:

1. Remove the `throw new NotSupportedException`
2. When there are multiple resources, return `null` (or the first resource)

But I need to also handle the property type resolution. Let me check if `CreateCSharpTypeCore` in `ProvisioningTypeFactory` can handle this by directly looking up resources from the output library, bypassing `CreateModel`.

Actually, let me look at this from the perspective of `ProvisioningTypeFactory.CreateCSharpTypeCore`. When resolving a model type, it can directly check if the model has resources and use the first resource's type:

```csharp
// In CreateCSharpTypeCore, for model types:
if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel)
{
    // Check provisioning mapping first
    if (KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(...)) return ...;
    
    // Check if it's a resource model with multiple resources
    var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
    if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(inputModel, out var resources) && resources.Count > 0)
    {
        return resources[0].Type; // Use first resource's type
    }
    
    // Fall through to base
}
```

But this would bypass the model creation entirely, which might cause issues with the `CreateModel` caching (models are cached after creation).

     6	using Azure.Generator.Provisioning.Providers;

    11	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Primitives;
    12	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Providers;
    13	using System;
    14	using System.Linq;
    15	
    16	namespace Azure.Generator.Provisioning
    17	{
    18	    /// <summary>
    19	    /// TypeFactory for provisioning generator that intercepts model/enum creation
    20	    /// to return provisioning-style type providers (ProvisionableConstruct/ProvisionableResource)
    21	    /// instead of management-style types.
    22	    /// </summary>
    23	    public class ProvisioningTypeFactory : ManagementTypeFactory
    24	    {
    25	        /// <summary>
    26	        /// Builds the resource provider name from the provisioning namespace.
    27	        /// For instance, "Azure.Provisioning.KeyVault" returns "KeyVault".
    28	        /// </summary>
    29	        protected override string BuildResourceProviderName()
    30	        {
    31	            const string provisioningNamespacePrefix = "Azure.Provisioning.";
    32	            if (PrimaryNamespace.StartsWith(provisioningNamespacePrefix))
    33	            {
    34	                return PrimaryNamespace[provisioningNamespacePrefix.Length..].ToIdentifierName();
    35	            }
    36	            return base.BuildResourceProviderName();
    37	        }
    38	
    39	        /// <inheritdoc/>
    40	        protected override CSharpType? CreateCSharpTypeCore(InputType inputType)
    41	        {
    42	            // For model types, check if there's a provisioning-specific type mapping first
    43	            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel
    44	                && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provisioningType))
    45	            {
    46	                return provisioningType;
    47	            }
    48	
    49	            // For enum types, check provisioning mapping too (e.g., ManagedServiceIdentityType)
    50	            if (inputType is InputEnumType inputEnum
    51	                && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputEnum.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provisioningEnumType))
    52	            {
    53	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), provisioningEnumType);
    54	            }
    55	
    56	            // Let the mgmt base resolve known system types (ResourceIdentifier, AzureLocation, etc.)
    57	            var mgmtType = base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
    58	
    59	            // For model types: if resolved to a system type that's a ProvisionableConstruct, return as-is.
    60	            // Otherwise, for non-ProvisionableConstruct system types (ResponseError from mgmt),
    61	            // wrap in BicepValue<T> since they can't be used with DefineModelProperty.
    62	            if (inputType is InputModelType)
    63	            {
    64	                if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
    65	                    && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
    66	                {
    67	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
    68	                }
    69	                return mgmtType;
    70	            }
    71	
    72	            // For enum types, wrap in BicepValue<T>
    73	            // System enums: mgmtType is the system CSharpType
    74	            // Non-system enums: mgmtType is our ProvisioningEnumProvider.Type
    75	            if (inputType is InputEnumType)
    76	            {
    77	                if (mgmtType != null)
    78	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
    79	                // Fallback: shouldn't happen now that ProvisioningEnumProvider is wired up
    80	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), typeof(string));
    81	            }
    82	
    83	            // For array types, produce BicepList<T> — element type should NOT be BicepValue-wrapped
    84	            if (inputType is InputArrayType arrayType)
    85	            {
    86	                var elementType = GetUnwrappedCSharpType(arrayType.ValueType);
    87	                if (elementType != null)
    88	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepList<>), elementType);
    89	            }
    90	
    91	            // For dictionary types, produce BicepDictionary<TValue> — value type should NOT be BicepValue-wrapped
    92	            if (inputType is InputDictionaryType dictType)
    93	            {
    94	                var valueType = GetUnwrappedCSharpType(dictType.ValueType);
    95	                if (valueType != null)
    96	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepDictionary<>), valueType);
    97	            }
    98	
    99	            // For all other non-model, non-enum types resolved by base (primitives, date/time, duration, etc.),
   100	            // wrap in BicepValue<T>
   101	            if (mgmtType != null)
   102	            {
   103	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
   104	            }
   105	
   106	            return mgmtType;
   107	        }
   108	
   109	        /// <summary>
   110	        /// Resolves an InputType to its raw CSharpType without BicepValue wrapping.
   111	        /// Used for BicepList/BicepDictionary element types which handle wrapping internally.
   112	        /// </summary>
   113	        private CSharpType? GetUnwrappedCSharpType(InputType inputType)
   114	        {
   115	            // For model types, check provisioning mapping first, then fall back to base
   116	            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel)
   117	            {
   118	                if (KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provType))
   119	                    return provType;
   120	                return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType) ?? CreateCSharpType(inputType);
   121	            }
   122	
   123	            // For enum types, check provisioning mapping first, then fall back to base
   124	            if (inputType is InputEnumType inputEnum)
   125	            {
   126	                if (KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputEnum.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provEnumType))
   127	                    return provEnumType;
   128	                return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType) ?? typeof(string);
   129	            }
   130	
   131	            // For all other types, use the base resolution (returns raw .NET type)
   132	            return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
   133	        }
   134	
   135	        /// <inheritdoc/>
   136	        protected override ModelProvider? CreateModelCore(InputModelType model)
   137	        {
   138	            // Known provisioning types (ManagedServiceIdentity, SystemData, etc.) → null (use framework type)
   139	            if (KnownProvisioningTypes.IsKnownType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId))
   140	                return null;
   141	
   142	            // Inheritable system types (TrackedResource, ProxyResource, etc.) → null
   143	            // Provisioning types use ProvisionableConstruct/ProvisionableResource as base, not ARM base types
   144	            if (KnownProvisioningTypes.IsInheritableSystemType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId))
   145	                return null;
   146	
   147	            // "Unknown" discriminator variants are for deserialization fallback in client SDKs.
   148	            // Provisioning types are write-only (compiled to Bicep), so we skip them.
   149	            if (model.IsUnknownDiscriminatorModel)
   150	                return null;
   151	
   152	            // Resource models → look up from output library's pre-created resource providers
   153	            var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
   154	            if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(model, out var resources))
   155	            {
   156	                if (resources.Count == 1)
   157	                {
   158	                    return resources[0];
   159	                }
   160	                // Multiple resources share the same model — not yet supported
   161	                throw new NotSupportedException(
   162	                    $"Model '{model.Name}' is shared by {resources.Count} resource types " +
   163	                    $"({string.Join(", ", resources.Select(r => r.Name))}). " +
   164	                    $"Multiple resources sharing the same model is not yet supported. " +
   165	                    $"See https://github.com/Azure/azure-sdk-for-net/issues/56733");
   166	            }
   167	
   168	            // Derived discriminated resource types → ProvisioningResourceProvider (derived path)
   169	            if (model.DiscriminatorValue != null && IsBaseChainResource(model))
   170	            {

with open("eng/packages/http-client-csharp-provisioning/generator/Azure.Generator.Provisioning/src/ProvisioningTypeFactory.cs", "r") as f:

# Fix 1: Replace the NotSupportedException throw with returning null
old_throw = '''                // Multiple resources share the same model — not yet supported
                throw new NotSupportedException(
                    $"Model '{model.Name}' is shared by {resources.Count} resource types " +

                    $"Multiple resources sharing the same model is not yet supported. " +

                // are already added via the Resources list in BuildTypeProviders.
                // Return null here so the model itself is not treated as a resource model,
                // preventing duplicate type generation. For property type resolution,
                // the first resource's type is used (see CreateCSharpTypeCore).
                return null;'''

                return mgmtType;
            }'''

new_model_section = '''            // For model types: if resolved to a system type that's a ProvisionableConstruct, return as-is.
            // Otherwise, for non-ProvisionableConstruct system types (ResponseError from mgmt),
            // wrap in BicepValue<T> since they can't be used with DefineModelProperty.
            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModelType)
            {
                // If base resolution returned null (e.g., model shared by multiple resources),
                // look up the resources directly and use the first resource's type.
                if (mgmtType == null)
                {
                    var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
                    if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(inputModelType, out var sharedResources) && sharedResources.Count > 0)
                    {
                        mgmtType = sharedResources[0].Type;
                    }
                }

                if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
                    && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
                {
                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
                }
                return mgmtType;
            }'''

if old_model_section in content:
    content = content.replace(old_model_section, new_model_section)
    print("Fix 2 applied: added multi-resource fallback in CreateCSharpTypeCore")
else:
    print("ERROR: Fix 2 could not find the expected string")
    sys.exit(1)

with open("eng/packages/http-client-csharp-provisioning/generator/Azure.Generator.Provisioning/src/ProvisioningTypeFactory.cs", "w") as f:
    f.write(content)

print("All fixes applied successfully!")

use warnings;

my $file = "eng/packages/http-client-csharp-provisioning/generator/Azure.Generator.Provisioning/src/ProvisioningTypeFactory.cs";
open(my $fh, '<', $file) or die "Cannot open $file: $!";
my $content = do { local $/; <$fh> };
close($fh);

# Fix 1: Replace the NotSupportedException throw with returning null
my $old_throw = '                // Multiple resources share the same model — not yet supported
                throw new NotSupportedException(
                    $"Model \'{model.Name}\' is shared by {resources.Count} resource types " +
                    $"({string.Join(", ", resources.Select(r => r.Name))}). " +
                    $"Multiple resources sharing the same model is not yet supported. " +
                    $"See https://github.com/Azure/azure-sdk-for-net/issues/56733");';

my $new_return = '                // Multiple resources share the same model — all resource providers
                // are already added via the Resources list in BuildTypeProviders.
                // Return null here so the model itself is not treated as a resource model,
                // preventing duplicate type generation. For property type resolution,
                // the first resource\'s type is used (see CreateCSharpTypeCore).
                return null;';

    $content =~ s/\Q$old_throw\E/$new_return/;
    print "Fix 1 applied: replaced NotSupportedException with return null\n";
} else {
    print "ERROR: Fix 1 could not find the expected string\n";
    exit(1);
}

# Fix 2: In CreateCSharpTypeCore, handle the multi-resource fallback
my $old_model_section = '            // For model types: if resolved to a system type that\'s a ProvisionableConstruct, return as-is.
            // Otherwise, for non-ProvisionableConstruct system types (ResponseError from mgmt),
            // wrap in BicepValue<T> since they can\'t be used with DefineModelProperty.
            if (inputType is InputModelType)
            {
                if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
                    && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
                {
                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
                }
                return mgmtType;
            }';

my $new_model_section = '            // For model types: if resolved to a system type that\'s a ProvisionableConstruct, return as-is.
            // Otherwise, for non-ProvisionableConstruct system types (ResponseError from mgmt),
            // wrap in BicepValue<T> since they can\'t be used with DefineModelProperty.
            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModelType)
            {
                // If base resolution returned null (e.g., model shared by multiple resources),
                // look up the resources directly and use the first resource\'s type.
                if (mgmtType == null)
                {
                    var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
                    if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(inputModelType, out var sharedResources) && sharedResources.Count > 0)
                    {
                        mgmtType = sharedResources[0].Type;
                    }
                }

                if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
                    && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
                {
                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
                }
                return mgmtType;
            }';

if (index($content, $old_model_section) >= 0) {
    $content =~ s/\Q$old_model_section\E/$new_model_section/;
    print "Fix 2 applied: added multi-resource fallback in CreateCSharpTypeCore\n";
} else {
    print "ERROR: Fix 2 could not find the expected string\n";
    exit(1);
}

print $out $content;
close($out);

print "All fixes applied successfully!\n";

                    $"Multiple resources sharing the same model is not yet supported. " +
                    $"See https://github.com/Azure/azure-sdk-for-net/issues/56733");
ENDTHROW

my $new_return = <<'ENDRETURN';
                // Multiple resources share the same model — all resource providers
                // are already added via the Resources list in BuildTypeProviders.
                // Return null here so the model itself is not treated as a resource model,
                // preventing duplicate type generation. For property type resolution,
                // the first resource's type is used (see CreateCSharpTypeCore).
                return null;
ENDRETURN

if (index($content, $old_throw) >= 0) {
    $content =~ s/\Q$old_throw\E/$new_return/;
    print "Fix 1 applied: replaced NotSupportedException with return null\n";
} else {
    print "ERROR: Fix 1 could not find the expected string\n";
    print "Looking for (first 100 chars): " . substr($old_throw, 0, 100) . "\n";
    exit(1);
}

# Fix 2: In CreateCSharpTypeCore, handle the multi-resource fallback
my $old_model_section = <<'ENDMODEL';
            // For model types: if resolved to a system type that's a ProvisionableConstruct, return as-is.
            // Otherwise, for non-ProvisionableConstruct system types (ResponseError from mgmt),
            // wrap in BicepValue<T> since they can't be used with DefineModelProperty.
            if (inputType is InputModelType)
            {
                if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
                    && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
                {
                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
                }
                return mgmtType;
            }
ENDMODEL

my $new_model_section = <<'ENDNEWMODEL';
            // For model types: if resolved to a system type that's a ProvisionableConstruct, return as-is.
            // Otherwise, for non-ProvisionableConstruct system types (ResponseError from mgmt),
            // wrap in BicepValue<T> since they can't be used with DefineModelProperty.
            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModelType)
            {
                // If base resolution returned null (e.g., model shared by multiple resources),
                // look up the resources directly and use the first resource's type.
                if (mgmtType == null)
                {
                    var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
                    if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(inputModelType, out var sharedResources) && sharedResources.Count > 0)
                    {
                        mgmtType = sharedResources[0].Type;
                    }
                }

                if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
                    && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
                {
                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
                }
                return mgmtType;
            }
ENDNEWMODEL

if (index($content, $old_model_section) >= 0) {
    $content =~ s/\Q$old_model_section\E/$new_model_section/;
    print "Fix 2 applied: added multi-resource fallback in CreateCSharpTypeCore\n";
} else {
    print "ERROR: Fix 2 could not find the expected string\n";
    exit(1);
}

open(my $out, '>', $file) or die "Cannot write $file: $!";
print $out $content;
close($out);

print "All fixes applied successfully!\n";
ENDOFSCRIPT

    16	namespace Azure.Generator.Provisioning
    17	{
    18	    /// <summary>
    19	    /// TypeFactory for provisioning generator that intercepts model/enum creation
    20	    /// to return provisioning-style type providers (ProvisionableConstruct/ProvisionableResource)
    21	    /// instead of management-style types.
    22	    /// </summary>
    23	    public class ProvisioningTypeFactory : ManagementTypeFactory
    24	    {
    25	        /// <summary>
    26	        /// Builds the resource provider name from the provisioning namespace.
    27	        /// For instance, "Azure.Provisioning.KeyVault" returns "KeyVault".
    28	        /// </summary>
    29	        protected override string BuildResourceProviderName()
    30	        {
    31	            const string provisioningNamespacePrefix = "Azure.Provisioning.";
    32	            if (PrimaryNamespace.StartsWith(provisioningNamespacePrefix))
    33	            {
    34	                return PrimaryNamespace[provisioningNamespacePrefix.Length..].ToIdentifierName();
    35	            }
    36	            return base.BuildResourceProviderName();
    37	        }
    38	
    39	        /// <inheritdoc/>
    40	        protected override CSharpType? CreateCSharpTypeCore(InputType inputType)
    41	        {
    42	            // For model types, check if there's a provisioning-specific type mapping first
    43	            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel
    44	                && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provisioningType))
    45	            {
    46	                return provisioningType;
    47	            }
    48	
    49	            // For enum types, check provisioning mapping too (e.g., ManagedServiceIdentityType)
    50	            if (inputType is InputEnumType inputEnum
    51	                && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputEnum.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provisioningEnumType))
    52	            {
    53	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), provisioningEnumType);
    54	            }
    55	
    56	            // Let the mgmt base resolve known system types (ResourceIdentifier, AzureLocation, etc.)
    57	            var mgmtType = base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
    58	
    59	            // For model types: if resolved to a system type that's a ProvisionableConstruct, return as-is.
    60	            // Otherwise, for non-ProvisionableConstruct system types (ResponseError from mgmt),
    61	            // wrap in BicepValue<T> since they can't be used with DefineModelProperty.
    62	            if (inputType is InputModelType)
    63	            {
    64	                if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
    65	                    && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
    66	                {
    67	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
    68	                }
    69	                return mgmtType;
    70	            }
    71	
    72	            // For enum types, wrap in BicepValue<T>
    73	            // System enums: mgmtType is the system CSharpType
    74	            // Non-system enums: mgmtType is our ProvisioningEnumProvider.Type
    75	            if (inputType is InputEnumType)
    76	            {
    77	                if (mgmtType != null)
    78	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
    79	                // Fallback: shouldn't happen now that ProvisioningEnumProvider is wired up
    80	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), typeof(string));
    81	            }
    82	
    83	            // For array types, produce BicepList<T> — element type should NOT be BicepValue-wrapped
    84	            if (inputType is InputArrayType arrayType)
    85	            {
    86	                var elementType = GetUnwrappedCSharpType(arrayType.ValueType);
    87	                if (elementType != null)
    88	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepList<>), elementType);
    89	            }
    90	
    91	            // For dictionary types, produce BicepDictionary<TValue> — value type should NOT be BicepValue-wrapped
    92	            if (inputType is InputDictionaryType dictType)
    93	            {
    94	                var valueType = GetUnwrappedCSharpType(dictType.ValueType);
    95	                if (valueType != null)
    96	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepDictionary<>), valueType);
    97	            }
    98	
    99	            // For all other non-model, non-enum types resolved by base (primitives, date/time, duration, etc.),
   100	            // wrap in BicepValue<T>
   101	            if (mgmtType != null)
   102	            {
   103	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
   104	            }
   105	
   106	            return mgmtType;
   107	        }
   108	
   109	        /// <summary>
   110	        /// Resolves an InputType to its raw CSharpType without BicepValue wrapping.
   111	        /// Used for BicepList/BicepDictionary element types which handle wrapping internally.
   112	        /// </summary>
   113	        private CSharpType? GetUnwrappedCSharpType(InputType inputType)
   114	        {
   115	            // For model types, check provisioning mapping first, then fall back to base
   116	            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel)
   117	            {
   118	                if (KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provType))
   119	                    return provType;
   120	                return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType) ?? CreateCSharpType(inputType);
   121	            }
   122	
   123	            // For enum types, check provisioning mapping first, then fall back to base
   124	            if (inputType is InputEnumType inputEnum)
   125	            {
   126	                if (KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputEnum.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provEnumType))
   127	                    return provEnumType;
   128	                return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType) ?? typeof(string);
   129	            }
   130	
   131	            // For all other types, use the base resolution (returns raw .NET type)
   132	            return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
   133	        }
   134	
   135	        /// <inheritdoc/>
   136	        protected override ModelProvider? CreateModelCore(InputModelType model)
   137	        {
   138	            // Known provisioning types (ManagedServiceIdentity, SystemData, etc.) → null (use framework type)
   139	            if (KnownProvisioningTypes.IsKnownType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId))
   140	                return null;
   141	
   142	            // Inheritable system types (TrackedResource, ProxyResource, etc.) → null
   143	            // Provisioning types use ProvisionableConstruct/ProvisionableResource as base, not ARM base types
   144	            if (KnownProvisioningTypes.IsInheritableSystemType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId))
   145	                return null;
   146	
   147	            // "Unknown" discriminator variants are for deserialization fallback in client SDKs.
   148	            // Provisioning types are write-only (compiled to Bicep), so we skip them.
   149	            if (model.IsUnknownDiscriminatorModel)
   150	                return null;
   151	
   152	            // Resource models → look up from output library's pre-created resource providers
   153	            var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
   154	            if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(model, out var resources))
   155	            {
   156	                if (resources.Count == 1)
   157	                {
   158	                    return resources[0];
   159	                }
   160	                // Multiple resources share the same model — all resource providers
   161	                // are already added via the Resources list in BuildTypeProviders.
   162	                // Return null here so the model itself is not treated as a resource model,
   163	                // preventing duplicate type generation. For property type resolution,
   164	                // the first resource's type is used (see CreateCSharpTypeCore).
   165	                return null;
   166	            }
   167	
   168	            // Derived discriminated resource types → ProvisioningResourceProvider (derived path)
   169	            if (model.DiscriminatorValue != null && IsBaseChainResource(model))
   170	            {

     1	// Copyright (c) Microsoft Corporation. All rights reserved.

     4	using Azure.Generator.Management;
     5	using Azure.Generator.Provisioning.Primitives;
     6	using Azure.Generator.Provisioning.Providers;
     7	using Azure.Provisioning;
     8	using Azure.Provisioning.Primitives;
     9	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Input;
    10	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Input.Extensions;
    11	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Primitives;
    12	using Microsoft.TypeSpec.Generator.Providers;
    13	using System;
    14	using System.Linq;
    15	
    16	namespace Azure.Generator.Provisioning
    17	{
    18	    /// <summary>
    19	    /// TypeFactory for provisioning generator that intercepts model/enum creation
    20	    /// to return provisioning-style type providers (ProvisionableConstruct/ProvisionableResource)
    21	    /// instead of management-style types.
    22	    /// </summary>
    23	    public class ProvisioningTypeFactory : ManagementTypeFactory
    24	    {
    25	        /// <summary>
    26	        /// Builds the resource provider name from the provisioning namespace.
    27	        /// For instance, "Azure.Provisioning.KeyVault" returns "KeyVault".
    28	        /// </summary>
    29	        protected override string BuildResourceProviderName()
    30	        {
    31	            const string provisioningNamespacePrefix = "Azure.Provisioning.";
    32	            if (PrimaryNamespace.StartsWith(provisioningNamespacePrefix))
    33	            {
    34	                return PrimaryNamespace[provisioningNamespacePrefix.Length..].ToIdentifierName();
    35	            }
    36	            return base.BuildResourceProviderName();
    37	        }
    38	
    39	        /// <inheritdoc/>
    40	        protected override CSharpType? CreateCSharpTypeCore(InputType inputType)
    41	        {
    42	            // For model types, check if there's a provisioning-specific type mapping first
    43	            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel
    44	                && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provisioningType))
    45	            {
    46	                return provisioningType;
    47	            }
    48	
    49	            // For enum types, check provisioning mapping too (e.g., ManagedServiceIdentityType)
    50	            if (inputType is InputEnumType inputEnum
    51	                && KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputEnum.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provisioningEnumType))
    52	            {
    53	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), provisioningEnumType);
    54	            }
    55	
    56	            // Let the mgmt base resolve known system types (ResourceIdentifier, AzureLocation, etc.)
    57	            var mgmtType = base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
    58	
    59	            // For model types: if resolved to a system type that's a ProvisionableConstruct, return as-is.
    60	            // Otherwise, for non-ProvisionableConstruct system types (ResponseError from mgmt),
    61	            // wrap in BicepValue<T> since they can't be used with DefineModelProperty.
    62	            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModelType)
    63	            {
    64	                // If base resolution returned null (e.g., model shared by multiple resources),
    65	                // look up the resources directly and use the first resource's type.
    66	                if (mgmtType == null)
    67	                {
    68	                    var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
    69	                    if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(inputModelType, out var sharedResources) && sharedResources.Count > 0)
    70	                    {
    71	                        mgmtType = sharedResources[0].Type;
    72	                    }
    73	                }
    74	
    75	                if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
    76	                    && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
    77	                {
    78	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
    79	                }
    80	                return mgmtType;
    81	            }
    82	            // Otherwise, for non-ProvisionableConstruct system types (ResponseError from mgmt),
    83	            // wrap in BicepValue<T> since they can't be used with DefineModelProperty.
    84	            if (inputType is InputModelType)
    85	            {
    86	                if (mgmtType != null && mgmtType.IsFrameworkType
    87	                    && !typeof(ProvisionableConstruct).IsAssignableFrom(mgmtType.FrameworkType))
    88	                {
    89	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
    90	                }
    91	                return mgmtType;
    92	            }
    93	
    94	            // For enum types, wrap in BicepValue<T>
    95	            // System enums: mgmtType is the system CSharpType
    96	            // Non-system enums: mgmtType is our ProvisioningEnumProvider.Type
    97	            if (inputType is InputEnumType)
    98	            {
    99	                if (mgmtType != null)
   100	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
   101	                // Fallback: shouldn't happen now that ProvisioningEnumProvider is wired up
   102	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), typeof(string));
   103	            }
   104	
   105	            // For array types, produce BicepList<T> — element type should NOT be BicepValue-wrapped
   106	            if (inputType is InputArrayType arrayType)
   107	            {
   108	                var elementType = GetUnwrappedCSharpType(arrayType.ValueType);
   109	                if (elementType != null)
   110	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepList<>), elementType);
   111	            }
   112	
   113	            // For dictionary types, produce BicepDictionary<TValue> — value type should NOT be BicepValue-wrapped
   114	            if (inputType is InputDictionaryType dictType)
   115	            {
   116	                var valueType = GetUnwrappedCSharpType(dictType.ValueType);
   117	                if (valueType != null)
   118	                    return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepDictionary<>), valueType);
   119	            }
   120	
   121	            // For all other non-model, non-enum types resolved by base (primitives, date/time, duration, etc.),
   122	            // wrap in BicepValue<T>
   123	            if (mgmtType != null)
   124	            {
   125	                return new CSharpType(typeof(BicepValue<>), mgmtType);
   126	            }
   127	
   128	            return mgmtType;
   129	        }
   130	
   131	        /// <summary>
   132	        /// Resolves an InputType to its raw CSharpType without BicepValue wrapping.
   133	        /// Used for BicepList/BicepDictionary element types which handle wrapping internally.
   134	        /// </summary>
   135	        private CSharpType? GetUnwrappedCSharpType(InputType inputType)
   136	        {
   137	            // For model types, check provisioning mapping first, then fall back to base
   138	            if (inputType is InputModelType inputModel)
   139	            {
   140	                if (KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputModel.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provType))
   141	                    return provType;
   142	                return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType) ?? CreateCSharpType(inputType);
   143	            }
   144	
   145	            // For enum types, check provisioning mapping first, then fall back to base
   146	            if (inputType is InputEnumType inputEnum)
   147	            {
   148	                if (KnownProvisioningTypes.TryGetProvisioningType(inputEnum.CrossLanguageDefinitionId, out var provEnumType))
   149	                    return provEnumType;
   150	                return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType) ?? typeof(string);
   151	            }
   152	
   153	            // For all other types, use the base resolution (returns raw .NET type)
   154	            return base.CreateCSharpTypeCore(inputType);
   155	        }
   156	
   157	        /// <inheritdoc/>
   158	        protected override ModelProvider? CreateModelCore(InputModelType model)
   159	        {
   160	            // Known provisioning types (ManagedServiceIdentity, SystemData, etc.) → null (use framework type)
   161	            if (KnownProvisioningTypes.IsKnownType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId))
   162	                return null;
   163	
   164	            // Inheritable system types (TrackedResource, ProxyResource, etc.) → null
   165	            // Provisioning types use ProvisionableConstruct/ProvisionableResource as base, not ARM base types
   166	            if (KnownProvisioningTypes.IsInheritableSystemType(model.CrossLanguageDefinitionId))
   167	                return null;
   168	
   169	            // "Unknown" discriminator variants are for deserialization fallback in client SDKs.
   170	            // Provisioning types are write-only (compiled to Bicep), so we skip them.
   171	            if (model.IsUnknownDiscriminatorModel)
   172	                return null;
   173	
   174	            // Resource models → look up from output library's pre-created resource providers
   175	            var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
   176	            if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(model, out var resources))
   177	            {
   178	                if (resources.Count == 1)
   179	                {
   180	                    return resources[0];
   181	                }
   182	                // Multiple resources share the same model — all resource providers
   183	                // are already added via the Resources list in BuildTypeProviders.
   184	                // Return null here so the model itself is not treated as a resource model,
   185	                // preventing duplicate type generation. For property type resolution,
   186	                // the first resource's type is used (see CreateCSharpTypeCore).
   187	                return null;
   188	            }
   189	
   190	            // Derived discriminated resource types → ProvisioningResourceProvider (derived path)
   191	            if (model.DiscriminatorValue != null && IsBaseChainResource(model))
   192	            {
   193	                return new ProvisioningResourceProvider(model);
   194	            }
   195	
   196	            // Regular models (including discriminated models) → ProvisioningModelProvider
   197	            return new ProvisioningModelProvider(model);
   198	        }
   199	
   200	        /// <summary>
   201	        /// Checks whether any model in the base chain is a resource model.
   202	        /// </summary>
   203	        private bool IsBaseChainResource(InputModelType model)
   204	        {
   205	            var outputLib = ProvisioningGenerator.Instance.OutputLibrary;
   206	            var baseModel = model.BaseModel;
   207	            while (baseModel != null)
   208	            {
   209	                if (outputLib.TryGetResourcesByModel(baseModel, out _))
   210	                    return true;
   211	                baseModel = baseModel.BaseModel;
   212	            }
   213	            return false;
   214	        }
   215	
   216	        /// <inheritdoc/>
   217	        protected override EnumProvider? CreateEnumCore(InputEnumType enumType, TypeProvider? declaringType)
   218	        {
   219	            // Known provisioning enums → null (use framework type)
   220	            if (KnownProvisioningTypes.IsKnownType(enumType.CrossLanguageDefinitionId))
   221	                return null;
   222	
   223	            // Regular enums → ProvisioningEnumProvider
   224	            return new ProvisioningEnumProvider(enumType);
   225	        }
   226	
   227	        /// <inheritdoc/>
   228	        protected override PropertyProvider? CreatePropertyCore(InputProperty inputProperty, TypeProvider enclosingType)
   229	        {
   230	            // Run base chain which creates property and applies visitor renames (e.g., etag → ETag).
   231	            var baseProperty = base.CreatePropertyCore(inputProperty, enclosingType);
   232	
   233	            if (inputProperty is not InputModelProperty inputModelProperty)
   234	                return baseProperty;
   235	
   236	            if (enclosingType is IProvisioningPropertyInfo infoProvider)
   237	            {
   238	                var info = infoProvider.GetProvisioningPropertyInfo(inputModelProperty);
   239	                if (info == null) return null;
   240	                var resolvedName = baseProperty?.Name ?? info.PropertyName;
   241	                var bicepType = info.TypeOverride ?? CreateCSharpType(inputModelProperty.Type);
   242	                if (bicepType == null) return null;
   243	
   244	                return ProvisioningPropertyProvider.Create(
   245	                    resolvedName, bicepType,
   246	                    info.IsOutput, info.IsRequired, info.BicepPath, info.DefaultValue,
   247	                    enclosingType);
   248	            }
   249	
   250	            return baseProperty;
   251	        }
   252	    }
   253	}
